Spectral operator\n\n| Item | Specification |\n|---|---|\n| Definition | $G[\\mathsf{T}](U)_{ab} = \\sum_k \\big( \\sum_{ij} U_{ia} U_{jb} \\mathsf{T}_{ijk} \\big)^2$ — one einsum + square + sum |\n| Domain | $U \\in \\mathrm{St}(7,n)$, $2 \\leq n \\leq 7$ (via QR of unconstrained $7 \\times n$); results hold for arbitrary non-orthonormal frames and arbitrary vacuum $H$ |\n| Output | $n \\times n$ symmetric, entrywise nonnegative; **hollow** iff $\\mathsf{T}$ is $(i \\leftrightarrow j)$-antisymmetric |\n| Invariant (proved, $n=3$) | Sum rule $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$ (exact; Perron–Frobenius + tracelessness) |\n| Invariant (conjectured, $n \\leq 7$) | $s_1 = \\sum_{i \\geq 2} s_i$; verified $\\leq 1.2 \\times 10^{-15}$ over 45,000+ frames; 0 violations |\n| Spectral rigidity | Geometric spectra exist only at $x = 1/T_{n-1}$ (k-bonacci reciprocal): 0.6180340 / 0.5436890 / 0.5187901 / 0.5086604 / 0.5041383 for $n = 3..7$ |\n| Realization status | $n=3$: theorem. $n = 4,5,6$: machine-zero residuals ($10^{-28}$–$10^{-32}$), 40/40 converged starts. $n=7$: NOT realized — 28/28 starts stall at residual $1.5 \\times 10^{-8}$, base $0.5049$ (open problem) |\n| Excluded outputs | Any geometric spectrum at $x \\neq 1/T_{n-1}$; all strongly hierarchical textures $(1, \\epsilon, \\epsilon')$, $\\epsilon + \\epsilon' < 1$; FN/Cabibbo textures identically |\n\n## 3. Model catalogue (ML study)\n\n| Model | Construction | Params | Verdict (5-seed, 1-std rule) |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| FreeMixer | $W_2 \\tanh(W_1 x + b_1) + b_2$, $3{\\to}9{\\to}1$ | 46 | Loses in-class 23/24 cells; wins out-of-class ($M(x)$ teachers) with $n_{\\mathrm{train}} \\geq 96$ |\n| TruncAssociator | readout of $G[\\tilde{\\mathsf{B}}]$, Stiefel frame | 31 | In-class: 11W/9T/0L vs FreeMixer |\n| ExactAssociator | readout of $G[\\mathsf{B}]$ | 31 | Ties TruncAssociator (0W/20T/4L) — exactness buys nothing |\n| ScrambledTensor | readout of $G[\\mathsf{R}]$, random antisym tensor | 31 | Ties ExactAssociator 23/24 — algebra not load-bearing |\n| StiefelSlice | linear $3{\\times}3$ frame slice, same readout | 31 | Ties the quartet |\n| layer.py original | $\\tilde M$ + SVD features, $\\mathrm{Linear}(12,\\cdot)$ | 104 | Legacy; excluded from headline results |\n\nShared readout: $\\hat y = w^\\top \\tanh(\\mathrm{flat}(x_a \\hat G_{ab})) + b$, $\\hat G$ max-normalized.\n**Mechanism verdict:** capacity/bottleneck effect is 24× larger than any between-tensor difference. The operative prior is *fixed input-independent mixing*, not octonion structure.\n\n## 4. Teacher catalogue\n\n| Teacher | $M^*$ source | Class |\n|---|---|---|\n| golden / golden_exact | locked near-golden frame, truncated / exact tensor | fixed-matrix (in-class) |\n| random_associator / random_exact | random frame + vacuum, truncated / exact | fixed-matrix (in-class) |\n| non_associator | frozen MLP $3{\\to}16{\\to}9$, $M^*(x)$ per sample | input-dependent (out-of-class) |\n| linear (Exp 1) | $y = X_{\\mathrm{rot}} (1, \\varphi^{-1}, \\varphi^{-2})^\\top + \\varepsilon$ | degenerate (all models tie) |\n\nSignal head (all): $y = w^{*\\top} \\tanh(\\mathrm{flat}(x_a M^*_{ab})) + b^* + \\varepsilon$, $\\varepsilon \\sim \\mathcal{N}(0, \\sigma^2)$.\n\n## 5. Training & search specification\n\n| Item | Value |\n|---|---|\n| Optimizer | Adam; lr 0.01 (ML), 0.02–0.03 (spectral search, cosine anneal for $n=7$) |\n| Epochs / steps | 400 (ML benchmarks); 1,500–15,000 (spectral) |\n| Precision | float32 (ML), float64 (spectral / theorem verification) |\n| Ladder objective | $\\sum_i ((s_{i+1}^2 - s_i s_{i+2})/s_1^2)^2 + \\mathrm{relu}(c - s_n/s_1)$ |\n| **Barrier rule** | $c$ MUST be $< (1/T_{n-1})^{n-1}$ (target's smallest rung). $c = 0.02$ silently excluded hexanacci ($x^6 = 0.0163$) — cost one false verdict |\n| Seeds | Fixed integer seeds throughout; per-cell paired data between models; 5 seeds/cell for verdicts |\n| Verdict rule | Win iff $|\\text{mean paired gap}| > 1$ std of gap; else tie |\n| Hardware | CPU only (4GB VRAM insufficient); minutes per experiment |\n| Console | ASCII only (Windows cp1252) — Greek letters crash prints |\n\n## 6. Verified performance envelope (ML)\n\n| Regime | Result |\n|---|---|\n| In-class (fixed-matrix teacher), scarce/noisy data | 31-param bottleneck models reach noise floor $\\sigma^2$; up to 2× lower test MSE than FreeMixer; never significantly worse at any tested cell |\n| In-class, abundant clean data | Statistical tie with FreeMixer |\n| Out-of-class ($M(x)$ teacher), $n_{\\mathrm{train}} \\geq 96$ | FreeMixer wins 5/5 seeds; bottleneck models plateau at irreducible approximation error (~0.06–0.09) |\n| Attribution | Advantage transfers to ANY capacity-matched fixed-mixing model (scrambled tensor, linear slice) — do not market as octonionic |\n\n## 7. Failure modes & gotchas (all encountered, all documented)\n\n1. **Vector-part truncation** breaks alternativity → non-hollow $G$ → all spectral\n   theorems void. `layer.py` and everything built on its tensor is truncated.\n   Exact tensor lives only in `mechanism_test.py::build_exact_assoc_tensor()`.\n2. **Convention mixing**: two Fano conventions in the codebase (§1). Tensors are\n   not interchangeable.\n3. **Barrier-excludes-target** (§5): check guard rails against the hypothesis.\n4. **Single-seed verdicts lie**: 12/25 sweep cells flipped under 5-seed\n   replication. Never report a boundary from one seed.\n5. **cp1252 console**: `sys.stdout.reconfigure(encoding=\"utf-8\")` (as in\n   `octonion.py`) or ASCII-only prints.\n\n## 8. Open problems (spec for future work)\n\n| ID | Statement | Suggested attack |\n|---|---|---|\n| OP-1 | Universal sum rule: octonionic $G[\\mathsf{B}]$ image lies in the extreme hollow stratum for all $n \\leq 7$ | $G_2$-invariants of $\\phi$, $*\\phi$ (Harvey–Lawson calibrations) |\n| OP-2 | Hexanacci non-realizability at $n=7$ (moduli $O(7)/G_2$, dim 7 vs 5 constraints — count says fits, algebra says no) | exact critical-point analysis on $O(7)/G_2$ |\n| OP-3 | Does $G[\\mathsf{R}]$ (scrambled, hollow) *attain* its allowed k-bonacci ladders? Decides whether attainment (not just rigidity) is octonion-specific | rerun `tribonacci_test.py` with $\\mathsf{R}$ — one afternoon |\n\n## 9. File map\n\n| Layer | Files |\n|---|---|\n| Exact algebra | `FINALFUCKINGTIME/octonion.py` (canonical); `mechanism_test.py` (torch port + checks) |\n| Spectral experiments | `fn_ladder_scan.py` (+results), `fingerprint_test.py` (retracted), `tribonacci_test.py` |\n| ML benchmarks | `benchmark.py`, `benchmark_nonlinear_trap.py`, `benchmark_sweep.py`, `benchmark_sweep_multiseed.py`, `mechanism_test.py` |\n| Data | `sweep_results.csv`, `multiseed_results.csv`, `mechanism_results.csv`, `fingerprint_results.csv` |\n| Write-ups | `SPECTRAL_LADDERS_PAPER.md`, `THEOREM_NOTE.tex/.md`, `PAPER.md`, `ONE_PAGER.md`, `quad_sheet.html`, `EQUATIONS.md` (this doc's companion), `RESULTS.md` (log), `HANDOFF.md` (closeout) |\n| Figures | `paper_figure_1.png`, `ladder_figure.png`, `sweep_plots.png` |\n\n# The k-Bonacci Spectral Ladders of the Octonion Associator\n\n**Abstract.** We describe a rigidity phenomenon in the spectral geometry of the octonion associator. For a frame of $n$ imaginary octonions $u_1, \\ldots, u_n$ and a vacuum direction $H$, the associator Gram matrix $M_{ab} = \\|[u_a, u_b, H]\\|^2$ is hollow (zero-diagonal), symmetric, and entrywise nonnegative — the first property a direct consequence of alternativity. For $n = 3$ this forces the exact singular-value sum rule $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$, so the only geometric ladder $(1, x, x^2)$ the operator can realize satisfies $1 = x + x^2$: the base is the inverse golden ratio, as a theorem. Numerically the pattern extends to a full family: the sum rule $s_1 = \\sum_{i \\geq 2} s_i$ holds at relative precision $10^{-15}$ on every sampled frame for all $n \\leq 7$ — although matrix theory ceases to enforce it at $n = 4$ — and unbiased gradient searches realize essentially all of that family exactly (to machine precision for $n \\leq 6$), at the reciprocal k-bonacci constants: golden ($n=3$), tribonacci ($n=4$), tetranacci ($n=5$), pentanacci ($n=6$). The terminal case $n = 7$, where the frame exhausts $\\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$, is a reproducible near-miss: searches stall at residual $\\sim 10^{-8}$ with base $0.5049$ against the hexanacci value $0.50414$. We state the universal sum rule as a conjecture (plausibly provable via $G_2$-invariance), record the $n=7$ non-realizability as an open problem, and note the phenomenological corollary: Froggatt–Nielsen-type mass hierarchies are strictly excluded from this operator class at every frame size.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Introduction\n\nThe octonions $\\mathbb{O}$ are the largest normed division algebra, and the unique one that is *alternative but not associative*: the associator\n\n$$\n[x, y, z] = (xy)z - x(yz)\n$$\n\nis nonzero in general, yet totally antisymmetric in its arguments (Artin's theorem), vanishing whenever two arguments coincide. This paper concerns a spectral consequence of that antisymmetry which, to our knowledge, has not been recorded: the associator's natural Gram matrices can only form *self-similar (geometric) spectra* at a specific countable family of bases — the reciprocals of the k-bonacci constants — and they realize essentially all of that family.\n\nThe object of study is the map sending an $n$-tuple (\"frame\") $u_1, \\ldots, u_n \\in \\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ and a fixed vacuum $H \\in \\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ to\n\n$$\nM_{ab}(U; H) \\;=\\; \\big\\| [u_a, u_b, H] \\big\\\\|^2, \\qquad a, b \\in \\{1, \\ldots, n\\}, \\quad n \\leq 7 .\n$$\n\nThis operator arose in an attempt to derive Standard Model fermion mass hierarchies from octonionic geometry, where the desired output was a Froggatt–Nielsen texture — a spectrum $(1, x, x^2)$ with Cabibbo-suppressed base $x = \\lambda^2 \\approx 0.05$. That program failed in an unusually instructive way: numerical scans found the operator *could* produce geometric spectra, but only at base $0.618\\ldots$, and optimization toward any other base stalled at large residuals. The failure is explained by the theorem below; the generalization to larger frames (§4) is new.\n\n## 2. Structure: the associator Gram matrix is hollow\n\n**Lemma 1.** *For arbitrary $u_1, \\ldots, u_n, H \\in \\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ — no orthonormality, no genericity — $M(U;H)$ is symmetric, entrywise nonnegative, and hollow ($M_{aa} \\equiv 0$), hence traceless.*\n\n*Proof.* Entries are squared norms (nonnegative). Alternativity makes the associator antisymmetric in its first two slots, so $[u_b, u_a, H] = -[u_a, u_b, H]$ (equal norms: symmetry) and $[u_a, u_a, H] = 0$ (hollowness). $\\square$\n\n### 2.1 Explicit form and manifest $G_2$-covariance\n\nFor any algebraic argument the one-line definition should be expanded. With $\\phi_{ijk}$ the Fano 3-form, $\\Phi = \\tfrac16 \\varepsilon \\phi$ its Hodge dual, and $A_{ijml} = [e_i, e_j, e_m]_l = -2\\,\\Phi_{ijml}$ the associator tensor, trilinearity gives\n\n$$\n[u_a, u_b, H]_l \\;=\\; \\sum_{i,j,m} u_a^{\\,i}\\, u_b^{\\,j}\\, H^{m}\\, A_{ijml},\n$$\n\nso the Gram matrix is an explicit quadratic form **in the vacuum**:\n\n$$\nM_{ab} \\;=\\; \\sum_{m,m'} H^{m} H^{m'}\\, Q^{(ab)}_{mm'}, \\qquad\nQ^{(ab)}_{mm'} \\;=\\; \\sum_{i,j,i',j'} u_a^{\\,i} u_b^{\\,j} u_a^{\\,i'} u_b^{\\,j'}\\, K_{iji'j'mm'}, \\qquad\nK_{iji'j'mm'} \\;=\\; \\sum_{l} A_{ijml}\\, A_{i'j'm'l} \\;=\\; 4 \\sum_{l} \\Phi_{ijml}\\, \\Phi_{i'j'm'l}.\n$$\n\nEach $Q^{(ab)}$ is positive semidefinite (a sum of squares), and the contracted tensor $K$ is precomputed in the reference implementation (`octonion.py::build_K_tensor`). Because $G_2 = \\mathrm{Aut}(\\mathbb{O})$ preserves $\\phi$, hence $\\Phi$ and $A$, the covariance is manifest at the level of this formula:\n\n$$\nM_{ab}(gU;\\, gH) \\;=\\; M_{ab}(U;\\, H) \\qquad \\text{for all } g \\in G_2,\n$$\n\nand with $H$ fixed the residual symmetry is the stabilizer $\\mathrm{Stab}_{G_2}(H) \\cong SU(3)$. Any algebraic attack on the sum-rule conjecture (§5) should proceed through the standard $\\varepsilon$–$\\phi$–$\\Phi$ contraction identities applied to $K$; we deliberately leave $K$ uncontracted here rather than quote those identities without independent verification.\n\n### 2.2 Fragility of hollowness\n\nHollowness is the load-bearing property, and it is *fragile*: it belongs to the exact algebra. Truncating octonion multiplication to its imaginary part — a natural-looking simplification, and one this project's companion machine-learning study made — destroys alternativity, produces a generic diagonal, and erases every result below. (That truncation initially produced a spurious \"refutation\" of the golden-ratio behavior; the episode is documented in the project log as a caution: structural claims about an algebra must be tested with the exact algebra.)\n\n## 3. The n = 3 theorem: golden rigidity\n\n**Lemma 2 (sum rule).** *A real symmetric $3\\times3$ hollow matrix with nonnegative entries has singular values obeying $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$.*\n\n*Proof.* Perron–Frobenius for the nonnegative $M$ gives $\\lambda_1 = \\rho(M) \\geq |\\lambda_i|$. If $\\lambda_2 > 0$, tracelessness gives $|\\lambda_3| = \\lambda_1 + \\lambda_2 > \\rho(M)$, a contradiction; so $\\lambda_2, \\lambda_3 \\leq 0$ and $s_2 + s_3 = -(\\lambda_2 + \\lambda_3) = \\lambda_1 = s_1$. $\\square$\n\nThe sign structure is a special case of Charles–Farber–Johnson–Kennedy-Shaffer (SIAM J. Matrix Anal. Appl. 34, 2013), who show hollow symmetric nonnegative $n \\times n$ matrices have between $2$ and $n-1$ nonpositive eigenvalues; at $n = 3$ this forces exactly two. Our contribution is the octonionic application:\n\n**Theorem 1 (Golden Rigidity for n = 3).** *At every frame and every vacuum, the singular values of $M(U;H)$ ($n=3$) satisfy $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$. If the normalized spectrum is geometric, $(1, x, x^2)$, then $1 = x + x^2$ — the defining equation of the golden ratio — so $x = \\varphi^{-1} = 0.618034\\ldots$, uniquely.*\n\n> **Corollary 1 (exact Froggatt–Nielsen obstruction).** ***No frame and no vacuum yield a geometric spectrum at any base $x \\neq \\varphi^{-1}$; in particular Cabibbo textures ($x + x^2 \\approx 0.053 \\neq 1$) are excluded identically, and so is every strongly hierarchical texture $(1, \\epsilon, \\epsilon')$ with $\\epsilon + \\epsilon' < 1$. Conversely, the operator carries a rigid parameter-free signature: in the sum-rule normalization, $m_1 = m_2 + m_3$.***\n\n**Uniqueness is one-directional, and should not be overread.** The golden spectrum is the unique *geometric* spectrum, not the unique spectrum: on the sum-rule surface $s_2 + s_3 = s_1$ the normalized spectra $(1, r, 1-r)$ form a one-parameter family, and the original random scan realized $r = s_2/s_1$ across essentially its full admissible range $[0.5006,\\, 0.9994]$. The theorem collapses the geometric *locus* to a point; it does not collapse the operator's spectral range. (Consistently, the frame moduli here are higher-dimensional than the one-dimensional spectral family, so non-geometric spectra are generic and the golden point is a measure-zero target that optimization nevertheless reaches exactly.)\n\nVerification: sum-rule deviation $\\leq 6.5 \\times 10^{-16}$ over 2000 random Stiefel frames; $\\sim 10^{-7}$ over 300 non-orthonormal frames with random vacua. The theorem retroactively explains every feature of the original scans — the clustering of incidentally-geometric random frames at base $0.6181 \\pm 0.004$, the zero optimization residual at $\\varphi^{-1}$, and the $\\mathcal{O}(10^{-1})$ floors at all other prescribed bases.\n\n## 4. The k-bonacci family: n = 4 to 7\n\nFor $n \\geq 4$ the matrix facts weaken: hollow symmetric nonnegative matrices with only two nonpositive eigenvalues exist for every $n \\geq 4$ (CFJK), and for those the sum rule fails. Whether it survives is a question about the *image* of the octonionic map, not about hollow matrices in general. Empirically it survives everywhere:\n\n**Observation 1 (universal sum rule).** *Over 5,000–20,000 random frames per size, $n = 4, 5, 6, 7$: $\\max_U \\big| s_1 - \\sum_{i\\geq2} s_i \\big| / s_1 \\;\\leq\\; 1.2 \\times 10^{-15}$, and no sampled frame has a positive subdominant eigenvalue.*\n\nGranting the sum rule, a geometric ladder $(1, x, \\ldots, x^{n-1})$ must satisfy $1 = x + x^2 + \\cdots + x^{n-1}$, i.e. $x = 1/T_{n-1}$ with $T_k$ the k-bonacci constant (the root in $(1,2)$ of $t^k = t^{k-1} + \\cdots + 1$). Gradient searches for self-similar spectra — objectives written purely as $s_{i+1}^2 = s_i s_{i+2}$, never referencing any k-bonacci number — find:\n\n| $n$ | constant | predicted base $1/T_{n-1}$ | achieved base | ladder residual | sum-rule violation (max) | starts | epistemic status |\n|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|\n| 3 | golden | 0.6180340 | 0.6180340 | $0$ | $6.5 \\times 10^{-16}$ | — | **theorem** |\n| 4 | tribonacci | 0.5436890 | 0.5436890 | $< 10^{-28}$ (typ.) | $9.9 \\times 10^{-16}$ | 24/24 | numerically exact |\n| 5 | tetranacci | 0.5187901 | 0.5187901 | $3 \\times 10^{-32}$ | $9.3 \\times 10^{-16}$ | 8/8 | numerically exact |\n| 6 | pentanacci | 0.5086604 | 0.5086604 | $1 \\times 10^{-30}$ | $1.0 \\times 10^{-15}$ | 8/8 | numerically exact |\n| 7 | hexanacci | 0.5041383 | 0.5048538 | $1.5 \\times 10^{-8}$ (stall) | $8.7 \\times 10^{-16}$ | 0/28 | numerically excluded |\n\nThe rows do not share epistemic status: only $n = 3$ is proved; $n = 4$–$6$ are numerical realizations at machine precision (a proof of attainment is open); $n = 7$ is a numerical exclusion whose first-order structure is analyzed below.\n\n![Figure 1: (a) the k-bonacci base family with realized values; (b) the realized geometric ladders on a log scale — self-similarity appears as straight lines.](ladder_figure.png)\n\n**Observation 2 (realization, $n \\leq 6$).** *The octonion associator realizes the geometric ladder exactly at $x = 1/T_{n-1}$ for $n = 4, 5, 6$, and random-start gradient flows toward self-similarity converge to it with high reliability.*\n\n**Observation 3 (the $n = 7$ near-miss).** *At $n = 7$ — where the frame is a full orthonormal basis of $\\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ and the effective moduli collapse to $O(7)$ modulo the 14-dimensional $G_2$ automorphism action — 28 random starts under two barrier configurations stall at residual $\\sim 1.5 \\times 10^{-8}$, ten orders above the machine-zero convergence obtained with identical machinery at $n \\leq 6$. Achieved bases cluster at $0.5049$–$0.5054$, systematically $\\sim 9 \\times 10^{-4}$ above hexanacci, with the deviation concentrated in the two smallest rungs, while the sum rule continues to hold at $10^{-16}$ on every solution. We read this as evidence that the exact hexanacci ladder is not realizable: the octonionic image approaches the ladder locus to within $\\sim 10^{-4}$ per rung and appears to miss it.*\n\n## 5. Open problems\n\n**Conjecture (universal sum rule).** For all $n \\leq 7$ and all $u_1, \\ldots, u_n, H \\in \\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$, the singular values of $M(U;H)$ satisfy $s_1 = \\sum_{i \\geq 2} s_i$; equivalently, the octonionic image lies in the extreme stratum (exactly one positive eigenvalue) of hollow symmetric nonnegative matrices.\n\nThis is *not* a matrix-theoretic fact for $n \\geq 4$; a proof should exploit the $G_2$-invariant structure of the associator — e.g., its expression through the fundamental 3-form $\\phi$ and its Hodge dual [7] — rather than entrywise arguments. A positive resolution would classify the stratum of hollow nonnegative matrices realized by octonions, which seems independently interesting.\n\n**Problem (hexanacci non-realizability).** Prove or disprove: no orthonormal 7-frame of $\\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ gives $M(U; H)$ a geometric singular spectrum. The moduli reduction to $O(7)/G_2$ (dimension $21 - 14 = 7$) against the $5$ ladder constraints suggests a dimension count is *not* the obstruction, making the observed near-miss more curious, not less. A first-order (Jacobian) analysis sharpens the problem: at three independently converged stall points, $\\|J^\\top c\\| \\sim 10^{-8}$ (true critical points), the constraint Jacobian is effectively rank $4$ of $5$ ($\\sigma_5/\\sigma_1 \\approx 10^{-3}$), and the residual aligns with the collapsed direction to $|\\cos| = 1.0000$, with an identical residual signature across seeds — four of the five ladder conditions are satisfiable, and the fifth is blocked to first order on what appears to be a single canonical critical manifold. The analytic question is thus concrete: identify that manifold and show the fifth constraint's differential vanishes along it identically (code: `jacobian_test_n7.py`).\n\n**Question (interpolation).** The realized bases decrease monotonically toward $1/2$ (the $k \\to \\infty$ limit of $1/T_k$). Does the family's terminal misbehavior at $n = 7$ reflect the exhaustion of $\\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ — i.e., is the k-bonacci realization a strictly sub-maximal-frame phenomenon in any alternative algebra?\n\n## 6. Methods\n\nAll computations use the exact octonion algebra (Fano-plane structure constants with scalar parts retained; the associator tensor $B_{ijk} = [e_i, e_j, e_7]_k$ is precomputed exactly, making $M$ a bilinear `einsum` in the frame — the associator is trilinear, so no approximation is involved). Frames are parametrized by unconstrained matrices mapped to Stiefel frames by QR; searches use Adam (learning rates 0.02–0.03, up to 15,000 steps, float64) on the scale-free self-similarity objective $\\sum_i (s_{i+1}^2 - s_i s_{i+2})^2 / s_1^4$ with a small-rung barrier set *below* the target ladder's smallest rung (an earlier barrier of $0.02$ silently excluded the hexanacci target, whose smallest rung is $0.0163$ — the kind of guard-rail error worth documenting). Sum-rule scans use 5,000–20,000 frames per size. Everything runs on CPU in minutes; code: `tribonacci_test.py`, `mechanism_test.py` (tensor construction with built-in sum-rule self-check), and the original `fn_ladder_scan.py`.\n\n## 7. Relation to other golden-ratio phenomena\n\nGolden ratios arise in $E_8$-adjacent settings (folding to $H_4$; the Ising-chain $E_8$ spectrum with $m_2/m_1 = \\varphi$) and pervade quasicrystal geometry. The mechanism here is unrelated and elementary: antisymmetry makes the matrix hollow, nonnegativity plus tracelessness pin the spectrum's sign pattern, and self-similarity then has a unique fixed point — $1 = x + \\cdots + x^{n-1}$. The k-bonacci constants enter through their defining polynomials, not through any lattice or root system. We flag the coincidence to prevent, rather than to encourage, deeper numerology.\n\n## References\n\n1. J. C. Baez, *The octonions*, Bull. Amer. Math. Soc. **39** (2002) 145–205.\n2. R. D. Schafer, *An Introduction to Nonassociative Algebras*, Academic Press, 1966.\n3. Z. B. Charles, M. Farber, C. R. Johnson, L. Kennedy-Shaffer, *Nonpositive eigenvalues of hollow, symmetric, nonnegative matrices*, SIAM J. Matrix Anal. Appl. **34** (2013) 1384–1400.\n4. C. D. Froggatt, H. B. Nielsen, *Hierarchy of quark masses, Cabibbo angles and CP violation*, Nucl. Phys. B **147** (1979) 277–298.\n5. M. Günaydin, F. Gürsey, *Quark structure and octonions*, J. Math. Phys. **14** (1973) 1651–1667.\n6. R. Coldea et al., *Quantum criticality in an Ising chain: experimental evidence for emergent E8 symmetry*, Science **327** (2010) 177–180.\n7. R. Harvey, H. B. Lawson, *Calibrated geometries*, Acta Math. **148** (1982) 47–157. (The associative 3-form $\\phi$ and its coassociative dual, in the form used by Conjecture §5.)\n\n*Companion documents: `THEOREM_NOTE.tex` (physics-facing statement of the $n=3$ obstruction), `RESULTS.md` (full experimental log), `PAPER.md` (the machine-learning study in which this operator was originally embedded).*\n\n# An Exact Spectral Obstruction to Froggatt–Nielsen Ladders from the Octonion Associator\n\n**Abstract.** In octonionic approaches to flavor, a natural mass operator on a triple of generation vectors $u_1, u_2, u_3 \\in \\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ is the associator Gram matrix $M_{ab} = \\|[u_a, u_b, H]\\|^2$ against a fixed vacuum direction $H$. Numerical scans of this operator found that its normalized singular spectrum can form a geometric (\"Froggatt–Nielsen\") ladder $(1, x, x^2)$ only at the golden base $x = \\varphi^{-1} \\approx 0.618$, and that Cabibbo-like bases $x = \\lambda^2, \\lambda^4$ ($\\lambda \\approx 0.2243$) are unreachable at any frame. We prove both facts. Alternativity of the octonions forces $M$ to be symmetric with identically zero diagonal; since its entries are squared norms, $M$ is entrywise nonnegative and traceless, and Perron–Frobenius then yields the exact sum rule $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$ for its singular values, at every frame and every vacuum, with no orthonormality assumption. A geometric ladder is therefore possible only if $1 = x + x^2$, whose unique positive root is the inverse golden ratio. The appearance of $\\varphi$ in this operator class is thus a theorem rather than an emergent or fine-tuned feature, and the exclusion of hierarchical Cabibbo textures is exact: the program of deriving Froggatt–Nielsen hierarchies from this associator operator is closed, not merely unsuccessful.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Setup\n\nLet $\\mathbb{O}$ denote the octonions with imaginary units $e_1, \\ldots, e_7$ multiplying according to a fixed orientation of the Fano plane, and let $\\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O}) \\cong \\mathbb{R}^7$ be the imaginary subspace. The associator\n\n$$\n[x, y, z] \\;=\\; (xy)z - x(yz)\n$$\n\nmeasures the failure of associativity. Because $\\mathbb{O}$ is an *alternative* algebra — the subalgebra generated by any two elements is associative — the associator is a totally antisymmetric trilinear function of its arguments (Artin's theorem); in particular it vanishes whenever two arguments coincide, and for octonions it is purely imaginary.\n\nOctonionic and exceptional-algebraic structures ($J_3(\\mathbb{O})$, $E_6$) have long been proposed as organizing frameworks for one generation of Standard Model fermions, with the three generations associated to a triple of directions in $\\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$. In such constructions a candidate flavor operator, studied numerically in the program this note completes, is\n\n$$\nM_{ab}(U; H) \\;=\\; \\big\\lVert\\, [\\,u_a,\\, u_b,\\, H\\,] \\,\\big\\rVert^2, \\qquad a, b \\in \\{1, 2, 3\\},\n$$\n\nwhere $U = (u_1, u_2, u_3)$ is a triple (\"frame\") of imaginary octonions representing the generations and $H \\in \\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ is a fixed vacuum direction (e.g. $H = e_7$). The phenomenological target is a Froggatt–Nielsen (FN) texture: a normalized singular-value spectrum of the geometric form\n\n$$\n(s_1, s_2, s_3)/s_1 \\;=\\; (1,\\, x,\\, x^2),\n$$\n\nwith base $x = \\lambda^2 \\approx 0.0503$ (down-type) or $x = \\lambda^4 \\approx 0.0025$ (up-type), $\\lambda \\approx 0.2243$ the Cabibbo parameter.\n\nTwo robust numerical facts emerged from scans of this operator over the Stiefel manifold $\\mathrm{St}(7,3)$:\n\n1. Direct optimization toward geometric ladders converges, with residual at machine zero, to the **golden ladder** $(1, \\varphi^{-1}, \\varphi^{-2}) = (1, 0.618034, 0.381966)$, where $\\varphi = (1+\\sqrt5)/2$; among $8000$ random frames, all $859$ whose spectra were incidentally near-geometric (residual $<10^{-4}$) had base in $[0.614, 0.622]$, median $0.61810$.\n2. Optimization toward any *other* prescribed base — including both Cabibbo targets — stalls at residuals of order $10^{-1}$.\n\nThese facts were previously reported as an empirical anomaly: the operator \"prefers\" the golden ratio and \"refuses\" the Cabibbo hierarchy. We show both are consequences of a three-step argument requiring nothing beyond alternativity and the Perron–Frobenius theorem.\n\n## 2. The theorem\n\n**Lemma 1 (structure of $M$).** *For arbitrary $u_1, u_2, u_3, H \\in \\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ — no orthonormality or genericity assumed — the matrix $M_{ab} = \\|[u_a, u_b, H]\\|^2$ is symmetric, entrywise nonnegative, and has identically zero diagonal; in particular $\\mathrm{tr}\\, M = 0$.*\n\n*Proof.* Entries are squared norms, hence nonnegative. By alternativity the associator is antisymmetric in its first two arguments, so $[u_b, u_a, H] = -[u_a, u_b, H]$ and the two have equal norms: $M$ is symmetric. Antisymmetry likewise gives $[u_a, u_a, H] = 0$, so $M_{aa} = 0$. $\\square$\n\n**Lemma 2 (sum rule).** *Let $M$ be a real symmetric $3\\times3$ matrix with nonnegative entries and zero trace, and let $s_1 \\geq s_2 \\geq s_3 \\geq 0$ be its singular values. Then*\n\n$$\ns_1 \\;=\\; s_2 + s_3 .\n$$\n\n*Proof.* Let $\\lambda_1 \\geq \\lambda_2 \\geq \\lambda_3$ be the eigenvalues of $M$; since $M$ is symmetric, $\\{s_i\\} = \\{|\\lambda_i|\\}$. Because $M$ is entrywise nonnegative, the Perron–Frobenius theorem gives $\\lambda_1 = \\rho(M) \\geq |\\lambda_i|$ for all $i$, and $\\lambda_1 \\geq 0$. Suppose $\\lambda_2 > 0$. Then from $\\lambda_1 + \\lambda_2 + \\lambda_3 = 0$ we get $|\\lambda_3| = \\lambda_1 + \\lambda_2 > \\lambda_1 = \\rho(M)$, a contradiction. Hence $\\lambda_2 \\leq 0$, so $\\lambda_2, \\lambda_3 \\leq 0$, and\n\n$$\ns_2 + s_3 = -\\lambda_2 - \\lambda_3 = \\lambda_1 = s_1. \\qquad \\square\n$$\n\n**Theorem (golden rigidity).** *For every frame $U$ and vacuum $H$, the singular values of $M(U;H)$ satisfy $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$. Consequently, if the normalized spectrum is a geometric ladder $(1, x, x^2)$ with $x > 0$, then*\n\n$$\n1 \\;=\\; x + x^2 \\quad\\Longrightarrow\\quad x \\;=\\; \\frac{\\sqrt5 - 1}{2} \\;=\\; \\varphi^{-1},\n$$\n\n*and the ladder is $(1, \\varphi^{-1}, \\varphi^{-2})$: the defining equation of the golden ratio is imposed by the operator's structure.*\n\n**Corollary (exact FN obstruction).** *No frame and no vacuum realize a geometric ladder at any base $x \\neq \\varphi^{-1}$. In particular the Cabibbo textures are excluded exactly: for $x = \\lambda^2$, $x + x^2 \\approx 0.053 \\neq 1$; for $x = \\lambda^4$, $x + x^2 \\approx 0.0025 \\neq 1$. More generally, any target spectrum with $s_2 + s_3 \\neq s_1$ — which includes every strongly hierarchical texture $(1, \\epsilon, \\epsilon')$ with $\\epsilon + \\epsilon' < 1$ — is unrealizable by this operator class at any point of its domain.*\n\nThe sum rule is also the operator's positive prediction: any model in which physical mass parameters are identified (in some normalization) with the singular values of an octonion-associator Gram matrix of this type predicts the exact linear relation $m_1 = m_2 + m_3$ among the three normalized values. No observed fermion mass-squared or Yukawa hierarchy satisfies such a relation, which is an independent phenomenological statement of the obstruction.\n\n## 3. Numerical corroboration\n\nThe sum rule was verified to relative precision $6.5 \\times 10^{-16}$ over $2000$ random orthonormal frames, and to $\\sim 10^{-7}$ over $300$ frames drawn *without* orthonormalization and with random vacua $H$, confirming that neither orthonormality nor the choice $H = e_7$ is load-bearing. The theorem retroactively explains all reported scan phenomenology: the tight clustering of incidentally-geometric random frames at base $0.618$ (any frame near the geometric condition is necessarily near the golden point, the unique intersection of the constraint surface $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$ with the ladder family), the exact-zero optimization residual at base $\\varphi^{-1}$, and the $\\mathcal{O}(10^{-1})$ floors at every other prescribed base (the squared distance from the target ladder to the constraint surface).\n\n## 4. Scope and remarks\n\n**(i) What the mechanism needs.** The proof uses exactly two properties: the associator's antisymmetry under exchange of its first two arguments with a repeated-argument zero (alternativity), and the nonnegativity of squared norms. It therefore applies verbatim to the imaginary quaternions — where it is vacuous, since associativity makes $M \\equiv 0$ — and fails for generic non-alternative bilinear structures. Among the normed division algebras, the octonions are the unique case where the operator is both nonzero and constrained: the golden rigidity is, in this precise sense, an octonionic fingerprint.\n\n**(ii) A cautionary example.** The zero diagonal is destroyed by seemingly innocuous truncations. A companion machine-learning study implemented the associator keeping only the vector (imaginary) parts of intermediate products; the truncated operator is no longer alternative, its Gram matrix has a generic diagonal, and its self-similar spectra occur on a continuum of bases with no golden preference. A test of the golden property run against the truncated operator produced a spurious refutation before the discrepancy was traced. Structural claims about an algebra must be tested with the exact algebra.\n\n**(iii) Larger frames — the k-bonacci family (RESOLVED, see THEOREM_NOTE.tex §3).** For $n$-frames the matrix is again hollow, symmetric, nonnegative, but for $n \\geq 4$ matrix theory alone no longer forces the sum rule (hollow matrices with only two nonpositive eigenvalues exist; Charles–Farber–Johnson–Kennedy-Shaffer, SIAM J. Matrix Anal. Appl. 34 (2013)). Empirically the octonionic image satisfies $s_1 = \\sum_{i\\geq2} s_i$ universally (max deviation $10^{-15}$ over 5000 frames per size, $n \\leq 7$ — stated as a conjecture, plausibly provable via $G_2$-invariance), and gradient searches realize the geometric ladder **exactly at the reciprocal k-bonacci constants**: tribonacci $0.5436890$ ($n=4$, 24/24 starts), tetranacci $0.5187901$ ($n=5$), pentanacci $0.5086604$ ($n=6$), all at machine-zero residual. At $n=7$ (full basis of $\\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$; moduli collapse to $O(7)/G_2$) the searches stall at residual $\\sim10^{-8}$ with base $\\approx 0.5049$ vs hexanacci $0.5041$ — a near-miss read as evidence of genuine non-realizability, left open.\n\n**(iv) Relation to other golden-ratio appearances.** Golden ratios arise in $E_8$-adjacent contexts through the folding of the $E_8$ root system to the icosahedral group $H_4$, and famously in the $E_8$ mass spectrum of the critical Ising chain, where $m_2/m_1 = \\varphi$. The mechanism here is unrelated and far more elementary: no exceptional group, lattice, or integrability enters — only alternativity, nonnegativity, and the equation $1 = x + x^2$. We caution against reading deeper structure into the coincidence.\n\n## 5. Conclusion\n\nThe numerical observation that the octonion associator mass operator \"produces the golden ratio instead of the Cabibbo angle\" is a theorem: the operator's singular spectrum obeys the exact sum rule $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$ at every point of its domain, geometric ladders exist only at the golden base, and Froggatt–Nielsen hierarchies are excluded not approximately but identically. A research program seeking Cabibbo-like textures from this operator class can be closed with a proof rather than abandoned for lack of results. The residual positive content is twofold: a rigid, parameter-free spectral signature ($m_1 = m_2 + m_3$) that any future octonionic-associator mass model must either exhibit or evade by changing the operator, and a clean algebraic characterization — alternativity without associativity — of when such golden rigidity occurs at all.\n\n---\n\n## Reproducibility\n\nAll claims are verifiable with the accompanying code: `fn_ladder_scan.py` and `fn_ladder_scan_results.json` (original scans; sibling physics repository), `octonion.py` (exact algebra, verified on import), and `mechanism_test.py` (exact associator tensor with the sum-rule check `verify_exact_tensor()`). The sum-rule verifications reported in §3 run in seconds on CPU.\n\n# Associator Neural Layer: Empirical Status and Stiefel Control\n\n## Executive summary\n\nWe built a controlled benchmark suite to test whether an octonion / non-associative associator layer is a useful neural-network inductive bias.\n\nThe answer is **yes against unconstrained FreeMixer baselines on associator-family teachers**, but **not yet decisively yes for the uniquely octonionic contraction once a parameter-matched Stiefel control is introduced**.\n\nThe strongest supported claim is:\n\n> A 31-parameter geometric bottleneck based on a learned 7D/3D frame gives strong sample-efficient generalization on associator-family data and beats a larger 46-parameter unconstrained FreeMixer. The octonion associator contraction itself shows a small positive signal on random-associator teachers, but the current evidence does not yet isolate it as decisively superior to a non-octonion Stiefel control.\n\nThis is a useful result because it narrows the source of the advantage: the architecture is genuinely structure-matching, but the next experiment must make the octonion contraction more load-bearing.\n\n---\n\n## Files produced\n\nCore benchmark scripts:\n\n```text\nbenchmark_sweep.py\nbenchmark_sweep_repeated.py\nanalyze_assoc_vs_stiefel.py\n```\n\nTests:\n\n```text\ntests/test_benchmark_sweep.py\ntests/test_benchmark_sweep_repeated.py\ntests/test_assoc_vs_stiefel_analysis.py\n```\n\nFull sweep outputs:\n\n```text\nsweep_results.csv\nsweep_plots.png\nsweep_repeated_raw.csv\nsweep_repeated_summary.csv\nsweep_repeated_winrate.png\nassoc_vs_stiefel_pairs.csv\nassoc_vs_stiefel_summary.csv\nassoc_vs_stiefel_by_teacher.csv\nassoc_vs_stiefel_heatmap.png\n```\n\nImportant plots:\n\n```text\nsweep_plots.png\nsweep_repeated_winrate.png\nassoc_vs_stiefel_heatmap.png\n```\n\n---\n\n## Core hypothesis\n\nStandard neural-network layers are mostly built from associative matrix operations. Octonions are non-associative, so they expose the associator\n\n\\[\n[a,b,c] = (ab)c - a(bc).\n\\]\n\nThe benchmark asks whether a neural layer whose feature matrix is generated by octonion associator contractions can act as a stable, sample-efficient feature extractor.\n\nThe key question is not whether octonions beat all neural networks. The precise question is:\n\n> When the data-generating rule has associator-family structure, does an associator-constrained layer generalize better than unconstrained or parameter-matched alternatives?\n\n---\n\n## Teacher families\n\nEach teacher generates input/output pairs:\n\n```text\nX: (n_samples, 3)\nY: (n_samples, 1)\n```\n\nAll teachers share the same outer nonlinear form:\n\n\\[\nY = \\tanh(\\operatorname{features}(X, M))w + b.\n\\]\n\nThe difference is how the matrix/features are generated.\n\n### 1. `golden`\n\nA locked octonion associator teacher using the golden-ratio frame and fixed `e7` vacuum.\n\nPurpose:\n\n> Friendly sanity check: can the associator architecture recover the locked golden associator structure?\n\n### 2. `random_associator`\n\nA randomly seeded associator-family teacher with random 3-frame and random vacuum.\n\nPurpose:\n\n> Test whether the effect generalizes beyond the special golden frame.\n\nThis is the most important positive teacher.\n\n### 3. `non_associator`\n\nA frozen random MLP teacher:\n\n```text\nLinear(3,16) -> GELU -> Linear(16,9)\n```\n\nPurpose:\n\n> Negative control: does the associator fail when the hidden rule is not associator-structured?\n\nIt mostly does, which is good evidence that the bias is specific rather than universally overpowered.\n\n---\n\n## Models compared\n\n### `FreeMixer`\n\n```text\n46 parameters\n```\n\nAn unconstrained neural feature mixer.\n\nPurpose:\n\n> Larger, freer baseline.\n\n### `Associator`\n\n```text\n31 parameters\n```\n\nThe octonion associator model. It learns a 7D/3D frame and uses octonion associator contractions to produce its feature matrix.\n\nPurpose:\n\n> Main non-associative model under test.\n\n### `LowRankFreeMixer`\n\n```text\n31 parameters\n```\n\nA parameter-matched ordinary bottleneck.\n\nPurpose:\n\n> Tests whether the advantage is merely fewer parameters.\n\n### `FrozenRandomFeature`\n\n```text\n10 parameters\n```\n\nFrozen random features plus learned readout.\n\nPurpose:\n\n> Tests whether any nonlinear random feature map is enough.\n\n### `StiefelNonOctonion`\n\n```text\n31 parameters\n```\n\nA learned 7D/3D Stiefel-style frame with the same parameter count as the Associator, but without octonion associator contractions.\n\nPurpose:\n\n> Sharp control: tests whether the gain comes from octonionic non-associativity or from geometric frame regularization.\n\n---\n\n## First sweep: Associator vs FreeMixer\n\nThe first full sweep compared only:\n\n```text\nAssociator: 31 params\nFreeMixer:  46 params\n```\n\nGrid:\n\n```text\nteacher_type = [golden, random_associator, non_associator]\nnoise        = [0.0, 0.05, 0.15, 0.30]\nn_train      = [16, 32, 48, 96, 192]\nepochs       = 400\nn_test       = 2048\n```\n\nTotal:\n\n```text\n3 × 4 × 5 × 2 = 120 model trainings\n```\n\nMean test MSE:\n\n```text\nmodel              Associator  FreeMixer\ngolden                0.036470   0.057590\nrandom_associator     0.034090   0.058619\nnon_associator        0.109550   0.081276\n```\n\nInterpretation:\n\n```text\ngolden:             Associator wins\nrandom_associator:  Associator wins\nnon_associator:     FreeMixer wins\n```\n\nThis supports the basic structure-matching claim:\n\n> The Associator helps on associator-family teachers and loses on non-associator teachers.\n\n---\n\n## Full repeated/control sweep\n\nThe stronger sweep added repeated seeds and controls.\n\nGrid:\n\n```text\n3 teacher types\n4 noise levels\n5 train sizes\n5 repeat seeds\n5 models\n```\n\nTotal:\n\n```text\n3 × 4 × 5 × 5 × 5 = 1500 model trainings\n```\n\nMean test MSE:\n\n```text\nmodel              Associator  FreeMixer  FrozenRandomFeature  LowRankFreeMixer  StiefelNonOctonion\ngolden               0.036064   0.061389             0.051252          0.055024            0.035422\nrandom_associator    0.034214   0.056397             0.040566          0.055833            0.035110\nnon_associator       0.111768   0.102926             0.115039          0.090722            0.113174\n```\n\n### Against FreeMixer\n\nThe Associator clearly beats FreeMixer on associator-family data:\n\n```text\ngolden:\n  Associator 0.036064\n  FreeMixer  0.061389\n\nrandom_associator:\n  Associator 0.034214\n  FreeMixer  0.056397\n```\n\nIt loses on non-associator data:\n\n```text\nnon_associator:\n  Associator 0.111768\n  FreeMixer  0.102926\n```\n\nThis is the desired boundary behavior.\n\n### Against LowRankFreeMixer\n\nThe Associator beats the parameter-matched low-rank control on associator-family teachers:\n\n```text\ngolden:\n  Associator       0.036064\n  LowRankFreeMixer 0.055024\n\nrandom_associator:\n  Associator       0.034214\n  LowRankFreeMixer 0.055833\n```\n\nBut LowRankFreeMixer wins on the non-associator teacher:\n\n```text\nnon_associator:\n  LowRankFreeMixer 0.090722\n  Associator       0.111768\n```\n\nAgain: useful structural bias, not universal superiority.\n\n### Against StiefelNonOctonion\n\nThis is the sharpest control.\n\n```text\ngolden:\n  Associator         0.036064\n  StiefelNonOctonion 0.035422\n\nrandom_associator:\n  Associator         0.034214\n  StiefelNonOctonion 0.035110\n\nnon_associator:\n  Associator         0.111768\n  StiefelNonOctonion 0.113174\n```\n\nThe Associator and Stiefel control are very close. This means the FreeMixer advantage is real, but not uniquely octonionic by itself.\n\n---\n\n## Focused Associator-vs-Stiefel analysis\n\nWe then directly paired the 31-param Associator and 31-param StiefelNonOctonion models on every repeated condition.\n\nFor each paired run:\n\n```text\ndelta = Stiefel test MSE - Associator test MSE\n```\n\nSo:\n\n```text\npositive delta = Associator better\nnegative delta = Stiefel better\n```\n\nBy teacher:\n\n```text\nteacher_type        assoc_mean   stiefel_mean   mean_delta   assoc_wins / repeats   win_rate   sign_test_p\ngolden              0.036064     0.035422       -0.000643    40 / 100               0.40       0.056888\nrandom_associator   0.034214     0.035110        0.000896    55 / 100               0.55       0.368202\nnon_associator      0.111768     0.113174        0.001406    54 / 100               0.54       0.484118\n```\n\n### Interpretation\n\n#### `golden`\n\nStiefel is slightly better:\n\n```text\nStiefelNonOctonion 0.035422\nAssociator         0.036064\n```\n\nAssociator wins only:\n\n```text\n40 / 100 paired repeats\n```\n\nSo the octonion contraction is not better on the locked golden teacher.\n\n#### `random_associator`\n\nAssociator is slightly better:\n\n```text\nAssociator         0.034214\nStiefelNonOctonion 0.035110\n```\n\nAssociator wins:\n\n```text\n55 / 100 paired repeats\n```\n\nThis is the best signal for the octonion contraction, but it is weak:\n\n```text\nsign_test_p = 0.368202\n```\n\nSo the direction is favorable but not statistically decisive.\n\n#### `non_associator`\n\nAssociator slightly beats Stiefel, but this is not meaningful evidence for octonions because both are mismatched and LowRankFreeMixer is the best overall model.\n\n---\n\n## Final empirical conclusion\n\nThe data supports this claim:\n\n> A 31-parameter geometric associator-style bottleneck is a useful inductive bias on associator-family tasks. It beats a larger unconstrained FreeMixer and a parameter-matched LowRankFreeMixer on associator-family teachers, while losing on non-associator teachers.\n\nThe data does **not** yet support this stronger claim:\n\n> The octonion associator contraction itself is decisively superior to a non-octonion Stiefel frame control.\n\nThe honest status is:\n\n> The non-associative architecture works as a structure-matching inductive bias, but the current benchmark says much of the advantage comes from geometric low-dimensional frame regularization. The uniquely octonionic signal is present but small, clearest on `random_associator`, and not statistically decisive yet.\n\n---\n\n## What this means scientifically\n\nThis is not a failure. It is a useful narrowing result.\n\nWe started with:\n\n> Does an octonion associator layer help?\n\nThe answer became:\n\n> Yes, relative to unconstrained and low-rank baselines on associator-family tasks.\n\nThen we asked:\n\n> Is the advantage uniquely octonionic?\n\nThe answer is:\n\n> Not yet proven. A Stiefel frame control captures much of the same advantage.\n\nSo the next benchmark must make the octonion part more load-bearing.\n\n---\n\n## Next decisive experiment\n\nThe current teachers collapse much of the associator structure into an induced 3×3 matrix. A non-octonion Stiefel model can approximate that too well.\n\nThe next test should use a teacher that depends on **multi-slot associator structure**, not only the final induced matrix.\n\nExamples:\n\n```text\n1. Teacher outputs explicit associator triple features [u_i, x, u_j].\n2. Teacher depends on bracket-order asymmetry: (ab)c versus a(bc).\n3. Teacher uses several vacuum slots / multiple associator contractions.\n4. Teacher produces vector targets that retain associator-channel information instead of scalar readout collapse.\n5. Dynamical-system benchmark where octonion associator terms are activated by multi-field or spatial perturbation structure.\n```\n\nThe decisive test should compare:\n\n```text\nAssociator\nvs\nStiefelNonOctonion\n```\n\nwith:\n\n```text\nsame parameter count\nsame learned frame dimension\nsame predictor\nonly contraction map differs\n```\n\nIf the Associator wins there, then the uniquely octonionic claim becomes much stronger.\n\n---\n\n## Bottom line\n\nWhat we have built is a working empirical lab bench for non-associative neural layers.\n\nCurrent result:\n\n```text\nAssociator-style geometric bottleneck: useful.\nOctonion-specific contraction: promising, not yet isolated.\n```\n\nBest current claim:\n\n> Non-associative octonion-inspired layers are useful structured feature extractors when the data has associator-family geometry, but the unique contribution of the octonion associator must be tested with more load-bearing associator teachers.\n\n# Equation Extraction and Unification\n\nEvery equation in the project, extracted with provenance (Part I), a single\nnotation standard (Part II), and the unified system rewritten in that notation\n(Part III) — ending with the structural observation the unification exposes.\n\n---\n\n## Part I — Raw extraction (grouped by source)\n\n### A. Exact algebra (`FINALFUCKINGTIME/octonion.py`, `THEOREM_NOTE.tex`)\n\n| # | Equation | Where |\n|---|---|---|\n| E1 | Oriented Fano triples: $(1,2,3), (1,4,5), (6,1,7), (2,4,6), (2,5,7), (3,4,7), (5,3,6)$ | `octonion.py` `ORIENTED_FANO_TRIPLES` |\n| E2 | Imaginary-unit product: $e_i e_j = -\\delta_{ij} + \\sum_k \\phi_{ijk} e_k$ | Fano table |\n| E3 | $\\phi_{ijk}$: totally antisymmetric, $=+1$ on cyclic orderings of E1 | `_build_phi` |\n| E4 | Hodge dual: $\\Phi_{ijkl} = \\tfrac{1}{6}\\, \\varepsilon_{ijklmnp}\\, \\phi_{mnp}$ | `_build_Phi` |\n| E5 | Associator: $[x,y,z] = (xy)z - x(yz)$ | `associator()` |\n| E6 | Associator tensor: $A_{ijkl} = [e_i, e_j, e_k]_l = -2\\,\\Phi_{ijkl}$ | `_build_A`, verified on import |\n| E7 | Alternativity (Artin): $[x,y,z]$ totally antisymmetric; $[x,x,z] = 0$ | `THEOREM_NOTE` Lemma 1 |\n\n### B. The spectral operator (`fn_ladder_scan.py`, `mechanism_test.py`, `tribonacci_test.py`)\n\n| # | Equation | Where |\n|---|---|---|\n| E8 | Vacuum slice: $B^{H}_{ijk} = A_{\\,i\\,j\\,H\\,k}$ (default $H = e_7$) | `fn_ladder_scan.py` `B_H`; `mechanism_test.py` `B_EXACT` |\n| E9 | Trilinearity: $[u_a, u_b, H]_k = \\sum_{ij} U_{ia} U_{jb}\\, B^{H}_{ijk}$ | einsum `'ia,jb,ijk->abk'` |\n| E10 | Mass (Gram) matrix: $M_{ab} = \\big\\| [u_a, u_b, H] \\big\\|^2 = \\sum_k \\Big( \\sum_{ij} U_{ia} U_{jb} B^{H}_{ijk} \\Big)^{2}$ | all operator code |\n| E11 | Stiefel parametrization: $U = \\mathrm{qr}(W)$, sign-fixed, $W \\in \\mathbb{R}^{7 \\times n}$ | `frame_from_params` |\n| E12 | Normalized ratios: $r_i = s_i / s_1$, $s_1 \\geq \\cdots \\geq s_n$ singular values of $M$ | `ratios_from_frame` |\n| E13 | Geometric-ladder residual ($n=3$): $\\big(r_1^2 - r_0\\, r_2\\big)^2$ | `geometric_error_from_ratios` |\n| E14 | Target residual: $\\sum_i \\big(r_i - x^{\\,i}\\big)^2$ for prescribed base $x$ | `target_error_params` |\n| E15 | FN/Cabibbo bases: $x_{\\text{down}} = \\lambda^2$, $x_{\\text{up}} = \\lambda^4$, $\\lambda = 0.2243$ | `fn_ladder_scan.py` |\n| E16 | General ladder objective: $\\sum_{i=1}^{n-2} \\Big( \\dfrac{s_{i+1}^2 - s_i\\, s_{i+2}}{s_1^2} \\Big)^{2} + \\mathrm{relu}\\!\\big(c - s_n / s_1\\big)$, barrier $c < x^{\\,n-1}$ | `tribonacci_test.py` (barrier lesson: $c = 0.02$ excluded hexanacci's $x^6 = 0.0163$) |\n| E17 | Self-similarity (fingerprint) objective: $\\big(s_2/s_1 - s_3/s_2\\big)^2$ | `fingerprint_test.py` (retracted context) |\n\n### C. The theorem chain (`THEOREM_NOTE.tex`, `SPECTRAL_LADDERS_PAPER.md`)\n\n| # | Equation | Where |\n|---|---|---|\n| E18 | Hollowness: $M_{aa} \\equiv 0$, $M_{ab} = M_{ba} \\geq 0$, $\\operatorname{tr} M = 0$ | Lemma 1 |\n| E19 | Perron–Frobenius: $\\lambda_1 = \\rho(M) \\geq |\\lambda_i|$, $\\lambda_1 \\geq 0$ | Lemma 2 |\n| E20 | Sign pattern: $\\lambda_2, \\lambda_3 \\leq 0$ (n=3; CFJK for general hollow bounds) | Lemma 2 / CFJK 2013 |\n| E21 | **Sum rule**: $s_1 = \\sum_{i \\geq 2} s_i$ | Theorem 1 (proved n=3; conjectured all $n \\leq 7$) |\n| E22 | Ladder ansatz: $(s_1, \\ldots, s_n)/s_1 = (1, x, x^2, \\ldots, x^{n-1})$ | Theorem 1 / §4 |\n| E23 | **Rigidity equation**: $1 = x + x^2 + \\cdots + x^{n-1}$ | Theorem 1, k-bonacci section |\n| E24 | Golden case ($n=3$): $1 = x + x^2 \\Rightarrow x = \\varphi^{-1} = \\tfrac{\\sqrt5 - 1}{2}$, $\\varphi = \\tfrac{1+\\sqrt5}{2}$ | Theorem 1 |\n| E25 | k-bonacci constants: $T_k$ = root in $(1,2)$ of $t^k = t^{k-1} + \\cdots + t + 1$; realized base $x = 1/T_{n-1}$ | §4 |\n| E26 | Mass signature: $m_1 = m_2 + m_3$ (sum-rule normalization) | Corollary 1 |\n\n### D. Machine-learning models and teachers (`layer.py`, `benchmark_sweep.py`, `benchmark.py`, `mechanism_test.py`)\n\n| # | Equation | Where |\n|---|---|---|\n| E27 | Truncated product (vector part only): $(x \\circ y)_k = \\sum_{ij} x_i y_j \\phi_{ijk}$ | `layer.py` `_oct_mul` |\n| E28 | Truncated defect: $\\tilde D_{ab} = (u_a \\circ u_b) \\circ V - u_a \\circ (u_b \\circ V)$; $\\tilde M_{ab} = \\|\\tilde D_{ab}\\|^2$ | `layer.py` forward |\n| E29 | `layer.py` model (104p): $u_i = W_i x + b_i$ ($3 \\to 7$, $i = 1,2,3$); features $= [\\mathrm{flat}(\\tilde M),\\, \\mathrm{svdvals}(\\tilde M)] \\in \\mathbb{R}^{12}$; $\\hat y = W_o f + b_o$ | `layer.py` |\n| E30 | Strict Associator (31p): $\\hat y = w^\\top \\tanh\\!\\big(\\mathrm{flat}(x_a \\hat M_{ab})\\big) + b$, $\\hat M = M / \\max_{ab}|M_{ab}|$, $U = \\mathrm{qr}(W)$ | `benchmark_sweep.py` |\n| E31 | FreeMixer baseline (46p): $\\hat y = W_2 \\tanh(W_1 x + b_1) + b_2$ | `benchmark_sweep.py` |\n| E32 | Teacher signal: $y = w^{*\\top} \\tanh\\!\\big(\\mathrm{flat}(x_a M^{*}_{ab})\\big) + b^{*} + \\varepsilon$, $\\varepsilon \\sim \\mathcal{N}(0, \\sigma^2)$ | `TeacherFactory._signal` |\n| E33 | Exp-1 linear teacher: $y = X_{\\mathrm{rot}} \\cdot (1, \\varphi^{-1}, \\varphi^{-2})^\\top + \\varepsilon$ | `benchmark.py` |\n| E34 | Exp-2 trap teacher: $y = M_{12} M_{23} - \\tfrac{1}{2} M_{13}^2$ (standardized) | `benchmark_nonlinear_trap.py` |\n| E35 | Golden regularizer: $\\mathcal{L}_{\\mathrm{reg}} = \\big(\\sigma_2/\\sigma_1 - \\varphi^{-1}\\big)^2 + \\big(\\sigma_3/\\sigma_2 - \\varphi^{-1}\\big)^2$; $\\mathcal{L} = \\mathrm{MSE} + 0.5\\, \\mathcal{L}_{\\mathrm{reg}}$ | `benchmark.py` |\n| E36 | Scrambled control tensor: $R \\leftarrow \\tfrac12 (R - R^{(i \\leftrightarrow j)})$, scaled to $\\|B^{H}\\|_F$ | `mechanism_test.py` |\n\n---\n\n## Part II — Unified notation\n\n| Symbol | Meaning | Replaces |\n|---|---|---|\n| $\\phi_{ijk}$ | Fano 3-form (E3) | `C_ijk`, `T`, structure constants |\n| $A_{ijkl} = -2\\Phi_{ijkl}$ | exact associator tensor (E4–E6) | `A`, `_A` |\n| $\\mathsf{T}$ | a generic *slot tensor* $\\in \\mathbb{R}^{7\\times7\\times7}$ | `B_H`, `B_EXACT`, `R`, `T` (layer.py) |\n| $\\mathsf{B} := B^{e_7}$ | the exact slot tensor, $\\mathsf{B}_{ijk} = A_{ij7k}$ (E8) | `B_H`, `B_EXACT` |\n| $\\tilde{\\mathsf{B}}$ | truncated slot tensor, $\\tilde{\\mathsf{B}}_{ijk} = [\\,e_i, e_j, e_7\\,]^{\\circ}_k$ via E27–E28 | layer.py operator (implicitly) |\n| $\\mathsf{R}$ | scrambled slot tensor (E36) | `ScrambledTensor.B` |\n| $U \\in \\mathrm{St}(7,n)$ | frame, $n \\leq 7$; columns $u_a$ | frames, 3-frames, `raw_frame` after QR |\n| $G[\\mathsf{T}](U)$ | **the Gram functional** — see U2 | $M$, $\\tilde M$, `mass_matrix`, `operator_matrix` |\n| $s_1 \\geq \\cdots \\geq s_n$ | singular values of $G$ | `sv`, `svdvals`, $\\sigma_i$ |\n| $P_n(x) = x + x^2 + \\cdots + x^{n-1} - 1$ | rigidity polynomial | E23, E24 |\n| $T_k$ | k-bonacci constant | E25 |\n| $\\varphi$ | golden ratio $= T_2$-analogue: $1/T_2 = \\varphi^{-1}$ | phi |\n\n---\n\n## Part III — The unified system\n\nEverything in the project is one functional evaluated at three different slot\ntensors, plus one matrix-theory fact.\n\n**U1 (slot tensors).** From the algebra, three tensors:\n\n$$\n\\mathsf{B}_{ijk} = A_{ij7k} \\;(\\text{exact}), \\qquad\n\\tilde{\\mathsf{B}}_{ijk} = \\big[(e_i \\circ e_j) \\circ e_7 - e_i \\circ (e_j \\circ e_7)\\big]_k \\;(\\text{truncated}), \\qquad\n\\mathsf{R} \\;(\\text{scrambled, } (i \\leftrightarrow j)\\text{-antisymmetrized}).\n$$\n\n**U2 (the Gram functional).** For any slot tensor $\\mathsf{T}$ and frame $U \\in \\mathrm{St}(7,n)$:\n\n$$\nG[\\mathsf{T}](U)_{ab} \\;=\\; \\sum_{k}\\Big(\\sum_{ij} U_{ia} U_{jb}\\, \\mathsf{T}_{ijk}\\Big)^{2}.\n$$\n\nThis single expression is E10 ($\\mathsf{T} = \\mathsf{B}$), the layer.py/ML operator\n($\\mathsf{T} = \\tilde{\\mathsf{B}}$; E27–E28 collapse to it by bilinearity of $\\circ$),\nand the mechanism-test control ($\\mathsf{T} = \\mathsf{R}$). Every model, teacher,\nand scan in the project evaluates $G$ at one of U1's tensors.\n\n**U3 (hollowness criterion).** $G[\\mathsf{T}]$ is symmetric and entrywise\nnonnegative for every $\\mathsf{T}$ antisymmetric in $(i,j)$; it is *hollow*\n($G_{aa} \\equiv 0$) **iff** $\\mathsf{T}_{ijk} = -\\mathsf{T}_{jik}$, since\n$G_{aa} = \\sum_k (\\langle u_a \\otimes u_a, \\mathsf{T}_{\\cdot\\cdot k}\\rangle)^2$\nvanishes exactly when each slice annihilates symmetric tensors.\n\n- $\\mathsf{B}$: antisymmetric (alternativity, E7) → hollow. ✔\n- $\\mathsf{R}$: antisymmetric by construction (E36) → hollow. ✔\n- $\\tilde{\\mathsf{B}}$: **not** antisymmetric ($e_i \\circ e_i = 0$ kills one term\n  but not the other) → generic diagonal. ✘\n\n**U4 (rigidity theorem, unified).** If $G$ is hollow (U3), then it is symmetric,\nnonnegative, traceless; for $n = 3$, Perron–Frobenius forces\n$\\lambda_2, \\lambda_3 \\leq 0$ (E19–E20, CFJK) and hence the sum rule\n\n$$\ns_1 = \\sum_{i \\geq 2} s_i \\qquad \\text{(E21)} .\n$$\n\nA geometric spectrum $(1, x, \\ldots, x^{n-1})$ (E22) is then possible only at\nthe root of the rigidity polynomial:\n\n$$\nP_n(x) = 0\n\\quad\\Longleftrightarrow\\quad\nx = 1/T_{n-1}\n\\qquad \\big(n{=}3\\!: x = \\varphi^{-1}\\big) . \\qquad \\text{(E23–E25)}\n$$\n\n**U5 (realization, empirical).** For $\\mathsf{T} = \\mathsf{B}$: the sum rule\nholds at $10^{-15}$ for all $n \\leq 7$ (conjecturally exactly), and $P_n$-roots\nare realized to machine precision for $n \\leq 6$; $n = 7$ near-misses at\nresidual $10^{-8}$. For $\\mathsf{T} = \\tilde{\\mathsf{B}}$: no sum rule, ladders\non a continuum of bases (the retracted fingerprint test, E17, measured exactly this).\n\n**U6 (the ML study, unified).** All models are readouts of $G$:\n\n$$\n\\hat y \\;=\\; w^\\top \\tanh\\!\\Big(\\mathrm{flat}\\big(x_a\\, \\hat G_{ab}\\big)\\Big) + b,\n\\qquad \\hat G = G / \\textstyle\\max_{ab} |G_{ab}|,\n$$\n\nwith $G = G[\\tilde{\\mathsf{B}}]$ (TruncAssociator), $G[\\mathsf{B}]$\n(ExactAssociator), $G[\\mathsf{R}]$ (ScrambledTensor), or replaced by a free\nmatrix / linear map (FreeMixer E31, StiefelSlice). Teachers (E32) are the same\nform with fixed $G^{*}$; the mechanism result says test error depends on the\n*form* of U6, not on which $\\mathsf{T}$ generates $\\hat G$.\n\n**U7 (losses).** Training: $\\mathcal{L} = \\frac1N \\sum (\\hat y - y)^2$\n$(+\\, 0.5\\, \\mathcal{L}_{\\mathrm{reg}}$, E35, optional$)$. Spectral search:\nE16 with barrier $c < 1/T_{n-1}^{\\,n-1}$.\n\n### The observation the unification exposes\n\nU3 + U4 say the rigidity theorem is a property of the **matrix class** (hollow,\nsymmetric, nonnegative), and the class is entered by *any* $(i \\leftrightarrow j)$-antisymmetric\nslot tensor — including the scrambled $\\mathsf{R}$. So in the sliced Gram form U2,\neven the non-octonionic control obeys golden/k-bonacci rigidity. What is\nspecifically octonionic is therefore **not the rigidity itself** but the fact\nthat a *natural, algebra-intrinsic* operator lands in the class: alternativity\nis what makes the honest nested associator (E5) antisymmetric, while its\ninnocent-looking truncation $\\tilde{\\mathsf{B}}$ falls out of the class. Three\npractical corollaries:\n\n1. The physics claim should be stated as: *octonions provide the canonical\n   natural example of the hollow-Gram class* (uniquely among normed division\n   algebras, E7 nonvacuously), not as: *only octonions produce golden spectra*.\n2. The realization results (U5, which bases are *achievable*) genuinely do\n   depend on $\\mathsf{T}$ — rigidity says \"only $1/T_{n-1}$ is allowed,\"\n   the algebra decides whether it is *attained*. Whether $G[\\mathsf{R}]$\n   attains its allowed ladders is a one-afternoon experiment nobody has run.\n3. This is the same lesson the ML mechanism test taught (U6): the class does\n   the work; the algebra picks the representative. The project's two halves,\n   restated in one notation, turn out to be the same finding.\n\n# HANDOFF: Non-Associative (Octonion Associator) Layer — Utility Study\n\nDate: 2026-07-09 (final revision — project closed)\nWorking directory: `D:\\Projects\\non_associative_ai_claude`\nSibling physics repo: `D:\\Projects\\FINALFUCKINGTIME` (exact algebra, original scans)\nHardware constraint: CPU only.\n\n---\n\n## 0.
