Framework}\\n\\\\author{Matthew Connelly}\\n\\\\date{11 July 2026}\\n\\n\\\\begin{document}\\n\\\\maketitle\\n\\n\\\\begin{abstract}\\nWe study a numerical and algebraic route for obtaining quark mixing from the compact moment map of a Freudenthal triple system over the exceptional Jordan algebra $J_3(\\\\OO)$.  Starting from two octonionic Jordan elements $J_u,J_d$ constructed from a shared seven-dimensional frame, we define sector states in the Freudenthal space\\n\\\\[\\n  \\\\Psi=(\\\\alpha,\\\\beta,X,Y)\\\\in \\\\FTS\\n\\\\]\\nand project their compact generation moment maps onto a Hermitian $3\\\\times 3$ observable.  We verify that the scalar slots $\\\\alpha,\\\\beta$ are inert for the generation $u(3)$ moment map, so scalar vacuum amplitudes alone cannot generate Cabibbo--Kobayashi--Maskawa (CKM) mixing.  We then show that a tau-real complex Jordan-slot ansatz,\\n\\\\[\\n  X_u=J_u+rJ_d,\\\\qquad Y_u=\\\\overline{X_u},\\n  \\\\qquad\\n  X_d=sJ_u+J_d,\\\\qquad Y_d=\\\\overline{X_d},\\n\\\\]\\ncan reproduce the observed CKM magnitudes and Jarlskog invariant to numerical precision for\\n\\\\[\\n  r\\\\simeq0.3887831255+0.2822870282i,\\n  \\\\qquad\\n  s\\\\simeq0.2372949892-0.5117538711i.\\n\\\\]\\nThis is a four-real-parameter diagnostic localization, not a derivation.  To test whether the fitted coefficients are selected by invariant dynamics, we implement the full Freudenthal quartic-gradient/attractor map $T(\\\\Psi)=\\\\Omega^{-1}d\\\\Delta(\\\\Psi)$ and examine self-attractor, coupled-plane, primitive fixed-charge, and primitive scalar-matched charge closures.  All direct attractor closures tested fail to select the CKM-fitting coefficients.  Thus the present work localizes the missing structure to complex two-Higgs-like Jordan-slot mixing, while establishing that generic $E_7/F_4$ orbit kinematics plus direct Freudenthal attractor closure is insufficient for a zero-parameter CKM derivation.\\n\\\\end{abstract}\\n\\n\\\\noindent\\\\textbf{Keywords:} exceptional Jordan algebra; Freudenthal triple system; CKM matrix; octonions; moment map; Jarlskog invariant; $E_7$; attractor equation.\\n\\n\\\\tableofcontents\\n\\n\\\\section{Introduction}\\n\\nThe observed quark mixing matrix is usually represented by the Cabibbo--Kobayashi--Maskawa matrix $\\\\VCKM$, whose small but nonzero complex phase is measured by the Jarlskog invariant $\\\\Jarl$ \\\\cite{Cabibbo1963,KobayashiMaskawa1973,Jarlskog1985,PDG2024}.  A long-standing theoretical question is whether the CKM hierarchy and CP phase can be derived from a deeper algebraic or geometric structure rather than fitted as free Standard Model parameters.\\n\\nExceptional Jordan and Freudenthal structures are natural candidates for such a program because $J_3(\\\\OO)$, the Albert algebra of $3\\\\times3$ Hermitian octonionic matrices, carries cubic norm, adjoint, and exceptional symmetry data related to $F_4$, $E_6$, $E_7$, and $E_8$ constructions \\\\cite{SpringerVeldkamp,McCrimmon,Krutelevich2004,BorstenDuffMarrani2012}.  The Freudenthal triple system $\\\\FTS$ built over $J_3(\\\\OO)$ carries a symplectic form and quartic invariant whose automorphism group is of type $E_7$.\\n\\nThis paper reports a targeted verification program around the following question:\\n\\n\\\\begin{quote}\\nCan a compact Freudenthal moment map, applied to octonionic Jordan data from a shared frame, reproduce or derive CKM mixing?\\n\\\\end{quote}\\n\\nThe answer is mixed.  The moment-map observable is rigid enough to localize a highly specific complex mixing mechanism.  However, the direct invariant state-selection and attractor equations tested here do not derive the necessary complex coefficients.\\n\\nThe central result is therefore deliberately modest:\\n\\n\\\\begin{center}\\n\\\\fbox{\\\\parbox{0.88\\\\linewidth}{\\nThe CKM matrix can be reproduced, to numerical precision, by complex tau-real mixing of two exceptional Jordan slots inside a Freudenthal state.  But the tested invariant Freudenthal attractor closures do not select the required coefficients.  The result is structural localization, not a zero-parameter CKM proof.\\n}}\\n\\\\end{center}\\n\\n\\\\subsection{Summary of contributions}\\n\\nWe make four concrete contributions.\\n\\n\\\\begin{enumerate}[label=(\\\\roman*)]\\n  \\\\item We formulate the compact generation moment map for Freudenthal states $\\\\Psi=(\\\\alpha,\\\\beta,X,Y)$ and reconstruct a Hermitian $3\\\\times3$ generation observable $H_\\\\Psi$.\\n  \\\\item We prove and numerically verify that the scalar slots $\\\\alpha,\\\\beta$ are inert for the $u(3)_{\\\\rm gen}$ projection.  Hence scalar vacuum amplitudes alone cannot change CKM eigenvectors in this observable.\\n  \\\\item We identify a complex tau-real Jordan-slot ansatz that reproduces CKM magnitudes and the Jarlskog invariant at the level of a diagnostic fit.\\n  \\\\item We implement the full Freudenthal quartic-gradient/attractor map and show that the natural direct attractor closures fail to select the CKM-fitting coefficients.\\n\\\\end{enumerate}\\n\\n\\\\subsection{Honesty boundary}\\n\\nThe numerical fit reported below has four real fitting parameters, namely $\\\\Re r,\\\\Im r,\\\\Re s,\\\\Im s$.  It is not a prediction unless an independent invariant principle selects $r,s$ without CKM data in the objective.  Sections~\\\\ref{sec:failed-actions} and~\\\\ref{sec:attractor} are included precisely to document which natural completion attempts fail.\\n\\n\\\\section{Exceptional Jordan and Freudenthal preliminaries}\\n\\\\label{sec:prelim}\\n\\nLet $\\\\OO$ denote the real octonion algebra and let\\n\\\\[\\n  \\\\JJ = J_3(\\\\OO)\\n\\\\]\\nbe the exceptional Jordan algebra of $3\\\\times3$ Hermitian octonionic matrices with Jordan product\\n\\\\[\\n  X\\\\circ Y = \\\\half(XY+YX).\\n\\\\]\\nWe use the trace pairing\\n\\\\[\\n  \\\\inner{X}{Y}=\\\\Tr(X\\\\circ Y).\\n\\\\]\\nThe Jordan adjoint $X^\\\\#$ is defined by the usual cubic identity\\n\\\\[\\n  X\\\\circ X^\\\\# = N(X) I,\\n\\\\]\\nwhere $N(X)$ is the determinant/cubic norm.  Equivalently,\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  X^\\\\#=X^2-(\\\\Tr X)X+\\frac{1}{2}\\\\left((\\\\Tr X)^2-\\\\Tr(X^2)\\\\right)I.\\n  \\\\label{eq:sharp}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nThe polarization of the adjoint is\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  X\\\\times Y=(X+Y)^\\\\#-X^\\\\#-Y^\\\\#.\\n  \\\\label{eq:cross}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\n\\nThe Freudenthal triple system over $\\\\JJ$ is\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\FTS = \\\\RR\\\\oplus \\\\RR\\\\oplus \\\\JJ\\\\oplus \\\\JJ,\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nwith elements written\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\Psi=(\\\\alpha,\\\\beta,X,Y).\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nThe symplectic form is taken as\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\Omega\\\\big((\\\\alpha,\\\\beta,X,Y),(\\\\gamma,\\\\delta,Z,W)\\\\big)\\n  =\\\\alpha\\\\delta-\\\\beta\\\\gamma+\\\\inner{X}{W}-\\\\inner{Y}{Z}.\\n  \\\\label{eq:omega}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nThe quartic invariant is\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\Delta(\\\\Psi)\\n  =A^2-4\\\\left[\\\\alpha N(X)+\\\\beta N(Y)-\\\\inner{X^\\\\#}{Y^\\\\#}\\\\right],\\n  \\\\qquad\\n  A=\\\\alpha\\\\beta-\\\\inner{X}{Y}.\\n  \\\\label{eq:quartic}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\n\\nFor complexified states we use the real structure\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\tau(\\\\alpha,\\\\beta,X,Y)=\\\\left(\\\\bar\\\\beta,\\\\bar\\\\alpha,\\\\bar Y,\\\\bar X\\\\right).\\n  \\\\label{eq:tau}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nA tau-real state satisfies $\\\\tau\\\\Psi=\\\\Psi$.\\n\\n\\\\section{Shared-frame Jordan data}\\n\\\\label{sec:frame}\\n\\nThe numerical gates use a shared orthonormal frame in $\\\\RR^7$, written\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  Q=(g_1,g_2,g_3,h_u,k_1,h_d,k_2)\\\\in SO(7).\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nThe first three vectors are interpreted as generation directions, while $h_u,h_d$ are two sector vacua.  For a vacuum $h$, define octonionic associator edge vectors\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  z(h)=[g_1,g_2,h],\\\\qquad\\n  x(h)=[g_2,g_3,h],\\\\qquad\\n  y(h)=[g_3,g_1,h].\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nFrom these, construct a Hermitian exceptional Jordan element\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  J(h)=\\n  \\\\begin{pmatrix}\\n  \\\\norm{y}^2+\\\\norm{z}^2 & \\\\bar z & \\\\bar y\\\\\\\\\\n  z & \\\\norm{z}^2+\\\\norm{x}^2 & \\\\bar x\\\\\\\\\\n  y & x & \\\\norm{y}^2+\\\\norm{x}^2\\n  \\\\end{pmatrix}.\\n  \\\\label{eq:jh}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nWe write\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  J_u=J(h_u),\\\\qquad J_d=J(h_d).\\n\\\\end{equation}\\n\\nThe frame used in the verification was obtained from the previously studied stationary action\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  S(Q)=\\\\Delta(1,\\\\widehat J_u,\\\\widehat J_d,1)-2N(\\\\widehat J_d)-\\\\frac12 P_{\\\\rm chiral}(Q),\\n  \\\\label{eq:frameaction}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nwhere hats denote norm-normalized Jordan elements.  The numerical stationary checkpoint was\\n\\\\begin{align}\\n  S&\\\\simeq -0.4736913740,\\\\nonumber\\\\\\\\\\n  \\\\Delta-2N_d&\\\\simeq -0.3521997982,\\\\nonumber\\\\\\\\\\n  \\\\Delta&\\\\simeq -0.1080838760,\\\\nonumber\\\\\\\\\\n  N_d&\\\\simeq 0.1220579611,\\\\nonumber\\\\\\\\\\n  P_{\\\\rm chiral}&\\\\simeq 0.2429831518.\\n  \\\\label{eq:framecheckpoint}\\n\\\\end{align}\\nThe frame construction is not claimed to be a final CKM derivation.  It supplies the shared octonionic arena in which the moment-map and attractor gates below are tested.\\n\\n\\\\section{Compact Freudenthal moment map}\\n\\\\label{sec:momentmap}\\n\\nLet $T\\\\in u(3)_{\\\\rm gen}$ act on the generation indices of the Jordan slots.  For compact probes we use $T=iA$, where $A=A^\\\\dagger$ is a Hermitian $3\\\\times3$ test matrix.  The compact moment map is\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\mu_\\\\Psi(T)=\\\\frac{i}{2}\\\\Omega(\\\\tau\\\\Psi,T\\\\Psi).\\n  \\\\label{eq:momentmap}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nThe Hermitian generation observable $H_\\\\Psi$ is reconstructed by the condition\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\Tr_3(H_\\\\Psi A)=\\\\mu_\\\\Psi(iA)\\n  \\\\label{eq:hreconstruct}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nfor all Hermitian $A$.\\n\\nFor two sector states $\\\\Psi_u,\\\\Psi_d$, diagonalizing $H_u,H_d$ gives unitary eigenbasis matrices $U_u,U_d$, and the observable mixing matrix is\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  V=U_u^\\\\dagger U_d.\\n  \\\\label{eq:mixing}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nThe absolute matrix $|V|$ and Jarlskog invariant\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\Jarl=\\\\left|\\\\Im\\\\left(V_{11}V_{22}\\\\bar V_{12}\\\\bar V_{21}\\\\right)\\\\right|\\n  \\\\label{eq:jarlskog}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nare compared to CKM data.\\n\\n\\\\section{Scalar-slot inertness}\\n\\\\label{sec:scalar-inertness}\\n\\nA first possibility is that the missing CKM degrees of freedom live in the scalar slots $\\\\alpha,\\\\beta$ of the Freudenthal state.  This is false for the compact generation projection.\\n\\n\\\\begin{proposition}[Scalar slots are inert for $u(3)_{\\\\rm gen}$]\\nAssume $T\\\\in u(3)_{\\\\rm gen}$ acts only on the Jordan/generation slots, so that\\n\\\\[\\n  T\\\\alpha=0,\\n  \\\\qquad\\n  T\\\\beta=0.\\n\\\\]\\nThen changing $\\\\alpha,\\\\beta$ cannot affect the reconstructed generation observable $H_\\\\Psi$ defined by \\\\eqref{eq:momentmap}--\\\\eqref{eq:hreconstruct}.\\n\\\\end{proposition}\\n\\n\\\\begin{proof}\\nThe scalar part of the symplectic form is\\n\\\\[\\n  \\\\alpha\\\\delta-\\\\beta\\\\gamma.\\n\\\\]\\nFor $T\\\\Psi=(0,0,TX,TY)$, the scalar contribution to\\n$\\\\Omega(\\\\tau\\\\Psi,T\\\\Psi)$ is therefore zero.  Thus $\\\\mu_\\\\Psi(T)$ depends only on the Jordan slots $X,Y$ and their response to $T$.\\n\\\\end{proof}\\n\\nThe numerical check over random scalar slots gave\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\max_{\\\\alpha,\\\\beta}\\\\norm{H_{(\\\\alpha,\\\\beta,X,Y)}-H_{(1,1,X,Y)}}=0\\n  \\\\label{eq:alphabeta-zero}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nwithin exact floating-point equality for the implemented probe.  Consequently, scalar amplitudes may matter for a larger state-selection problem, but not for the compact generation eigenvectors.\\n\\n\\\\section{Diagnostic complex Jordan-slot mixing}\\n\\\\label{sec:diagnostic}\\n\\nThe successful diagnostic ansatz is tau-real and mixes the two sector Jordan elements inside the Jordan slots:\\n\\\\begin{align}\\n  \\\\Psi_u&=(1,1,X_u,\\\\bar X_u),\\n  &X_u&=J_u+rJ_d,\\n  \\\\label{eq:psiu}\\\\\\n  \\\\Psi_d&=(1,1,X_d,\\\\bar X_d),\\n  &X_d&=sJ_u+J_d.\\n  \\\\label{eq:psid}\\n\\\\end{align}\\nA four-real-parameter search over $r,s\\\\in\\\\CC$ gives\\n\\\\begin{align}\\n  r&\\\\simeq0.3887831255168539+0.28228702817500606i,\\n  \\\\label{eq:rfit}\\\\\\\\\\n  s&\\\\simeq0.23729498924317205-0.5117538711322562i.\\n  \\\\label{eq:sfit}\\n\\\\end{align}\\nAt this point the moment-map reconstruction yields\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  |V|\\\\simeq\\n  \\\\begin{pmatrix}\\n  0.97435246&0.22499704&0.00369001\\\\\\\\\\n  0.22486405&0.97349226&0.04182082\\\\\\\\\\n  0.00856999&0.04109930&0.99911831\\n  \\\\end{pmatrix},\\n  \\\\label{eq:fitmatrix}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nwith\\n\\\\begin{align}\\n  \\\\norm{|V|-|\\\\VCKM|}_F&\\\\simeq 6.13\\\\times10^{-6},\\n  \\\\label{eq:fitfro}\\\\\\\\\\n  \\\\Jarl&\\\\simeq3.0765591558\\\\times10^{-5},\\n  \\\\label{eq:fitj}\\\\\\\\\\n  \\\\Jarl/\\\\Jarl^{\\\\rm target}&\\\\simeq1.0000000018.\\n  \\\\label{eq:fitjratio}\\n\\\\end{align}\\nThe extracted mixing angles were\\n\\\\begin{align}\\n  s_{12}&\\\\simeq0.2249985724,\\\\nonumber\\\\\\\\\\n  s_{23}&\\\\simeq0.0418211054,\\\\nonumber\\\\\\\\\\n  s_{13}&\\\\simeq0.0036900121.\\n  \\\\label{eq:angles}\\n\\\\end{align}\\n\\n\\\\begin{remark}\\nEquations \\\\eqref{eq:rfit}--\\\\eqref{eq:fitjratio} are a diagnostic fit.  They show where the missing structure must live if this framework is correct.  They do not, by themselves, prove that CKM has been derived.\\n\\\\end{remark}\\n\\n\\\\subsection{Comparison with insufficient ansaetze}\\n\\nSeveral nearby ansaetze fail.  A raw state\\n\\\\[\\n  \\\\Psi=(\\\\alpha,\\n  \\\\beta,J_u,J_d)\\n\\\\]\\nproduces a single real moment-map observable, not two sector observables.  Slot-separated real sector observables give\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  |V|\\\\simeq\\n  \\\\begin{pmatrix}\\n  0.99562284&0.09034180&0.02394843\\\\\\\\\\n  0.08918675&0.99497214&0.04556501\\\\\\\\\\n  0.02794445&0.04322968&0.99867427\\n  \\\\end{pmatrix},\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nwith Frobenius error $\\\\simeq0.195598$ and $\\\\Jarl=0$.\\n\\nA non-real independent-slot ansatz\\n\\\\[\\n  \\\\Psi_u=(J_u,rJ_d),\\n  \\\\qquad\\n  \\\\Psi_d=(sJ_u,J_d)\\n\\\\]\\ncan improve magnitudes but still gives no CP violation.  A representative best search had magnitude error $\\\\simeq0.010071$ but\\n\\\\[\\n  \\\\Jarl/\\\\Jarl^{\\\\rm target}\\\\simeq5.8\\\\times10^{-18}.\\n\\\\]\\nComplex interference inside the same Jordan slot is therefore essential.\\n\\n\\\\section{Two-Higgs interpretation of the fitted coefficients}\\n\\\\label{sec:higgs}\\n\\nThe coefficients in \\\\eqref{eq:rfit}--\\\\eqref{eq:sfit} naturally form a two-Higgs-like mixing matrix\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  C=\\n  \\\\begin{pmatrix}\\n  1&r\\\\\\\\\\n  s&1\\n  \\\\end{pmatrix}.\\n  \\\\label{eq:Cmatrix}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nThe fitted point has\\n\\\\begin{align}\\n  |r|&\\\\simeq0.48045633,\\n  &\\\\arg(r)&\\\\simeq0.6280146853\\\\simeq \\\\frac{\\\\pi}{5}-0.0003038454,\\n  \\\\label{eq:rgeom}\\\\\\\\\\n  |s|&\\\\simeq0.56409302,\\n  &\\\\arg(s)&\\\\simeq-1.1366165592.\\n  \\\\label{eq:sgeom}\\n\\\\end{align}\\nThe rephasing-invariant phase is\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\arg\\\\left(C_{11}C_{22}\\\\bar C_{12}\\\\bar C_{21}\\\\right)\\n  \\\\simeq0.5086018738.\\n  \\\\label{eq:rephasephase}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nFurthermore,\\n\\\\begin{align}\\n  \\\\det C&\\\\simeq0.7632822330+0.1319759722i,\\n  \\\\label{eq:detC}\\\\\\\\\\n  |\\\\det C|&\\\\simeq0.7746079166,\\n  \\\\label{eq:absdetC}\\\\\\\\\\n  \\\\arg\\\\det C&\\\\simeq0.1712130354.\\n  \\\\label{eq:argdetC}\\n\\\\end{align}\\nThe singular values of $C$ are approximately\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\sigma(C)\\\\simeq(1.51216322,0.51225153),\\n  \\\\qquad\\n  \\\\frac{\\\\sigma_1}{\\\\sigma_2}\\\\simeq2.95199358.\\n  \\\\label{eq:singularC}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\n\\nThis supports a concrete physical interpretation: the CKM phase is not attached to scalar Freudenthal amplitudes, but to the complex relative orientation of two Jordan/Yukawa structures.  In model-building language, the ansatz resembles a two-Higgs or GUT mixing matrix for primitive Yukawa sectors.  The problem is then to derive \\\\eqref{eq:Cmatrix}, not to tune it.\\n\\n\\\\section{Failed invariant state-selection actions}\\n\\\\label{sec:failed-actions}\\n\\nThe first completion attempt was to extend the frame action to a direct action for $r,s$.  Write\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  X=\\\\frac{J_u+rJ_d}{\\\\norm{J_u+rJ_d}},\\n  \\\\qquad\\n  Y=\\\\frac{sJ_u+J_d}{\\\\norm{sJ_u+J_d}}.\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nThe most direct analogue of the frame action is\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  S_{r,s}=\\\\Re\\\\left[\\\\Delta(1,1,X,Y)-2N(Y)\\\\right]-\\\\frac12 P_{\\\\rm moment}.\\n  \\\\label{eq:directSrs}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nAt the CKM-fitting point, the numerical gradient was\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\nabla S_{r,s}\\\\simeq(-0.3276,1.4626,-0.4019,-0.9533),\\n  \\\\qquad\\n  \\\\norm{\\\\nabla S_{r,s}}\\\\simeq1.82.\\n  \\\\label{eq:directgrad}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nThus the fitted point is not stationary.\\n\\nTable~\\\\ref{tab:failed-actions} summarizes the direct action and closure failures.\\n\\n\\\\begin{table}[h]\\n\\\\centering\\n\\\\begin{tabular}{p{0.46\\\\linewidth}p{0.38\\\\linewidth}}\\n\\\\toprule\\nCandidate & Result \\\\\\\\\\n\\\\midrule\\n$\\\\Re[\\\\Delta(1,1,X,Y)-2N(Y)]-\\\\frac12P_{\\\\rm moment}$ & CKM point not stationary; gradient norm $\\\\simeq1.82$ \\\\\\\\\\n$\\\\Re[\\\\Delta(1,1,X,Y)-2N(Y)]$ & CKM point not stationary; minimization goes to boundary \\\\\\\\\\n$\\\\Delta(\\\\Psi_u)+\\\\Delta(\\\\Psi_d)-\\\\frac12P_{\\\\rm moment}$ & selects almost-real coefficients; $\\\\Jarl\\\\simeq0$ \\\\\\\\\\nJordan-adjoint plane closure & best closure point real and identity-like \\\\\\\\\\nMutual sharp/dual closure & best point almost real; no CP \\\\\\\\\\n\\\\bottomrule\\n\\\\end{tabular}\\n\\\\caption{Direct invariant action and closure tests for deriving $r,s$.  Each test excludes CKM from the objective.  None selects the diagnostic coefficients \\\\eqref{eq:rfit}--\\\\eqref{eq:sfit}.}\\n\\\\label{tab:failed-actions}\\n\\\\end{table}\\n\\nThese failures motivate the full attractor test of the next section.\\n\\n\\\\section{Full Freudenthal attractor gate}\\n\\\\label{sec:attractor}\\n\\nThe Freudenthal quartic-gradient map $T(\\\\Psi)$ is defined by\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\Omega(T(\\\\Psi),\\\\delta\\\\Psi)=d\\\\Delta_\\\\Psi(\\\\delta\\\\Psi).\\n  \\\\label{eq:Tdef}\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nFor $\\\\Psi=(\\\\alpha,\\\\beta,X,Y)$ and $A=\\\\alpha\\\\beta-\\\\inner{X}{Y}$, the implemented components are\\n\\\\begin{align}\\n  T_\\\\alpha&=2A\\\\alpha-4N(Y),\\n  \\\\label{eq:Talpha}\\\\\\\\\\n  T_\\\\beta&=-2A\\\\beta+4N(X),\\n  \\\\label{eq:Tbeta}\\\\\\\\\\n  T_X&=-2AX-4\\\\left(\\\\beta Y^\\\\#-Y\\\\times X^\\\\#\\\\right),\\n  \\\\label{eq:TX}\\\\\\\\\\n  T_Y&=2AY+4\\\\left(\\\\alpha X^\\\\#-X\\\\times Y^\\\\#\\\\right).\\n  \\\\label{eq:TY}\\n\\\\end{align}\\n\\nWe tested general tau-real sector states with scalar slots,\\n\\\\begin{align}\\n  \\\\Psi_u&=(a_u,\\\\bar a_u,J_u+rJ_d,\\\\overline{J_u+rJ_d}),\\n  \\\\label{eq:attractorpsiu}\\\\\\\\\\n  \\\\Psi_d&=(a_d,\\\\bar a_d,sJ_u+J_d,\\\\overline{sJ_u+J_d}).\\n  \\\\label{eq:attractorpsid}\\n\\\\end{align}\\nThe diagnostic CKM point still gives\\n\\\\begin{align}\\n  \\\\norm{|V|-|\\\\VCKM|}_F&\\\\simeq1.0362\\\\times10^{-5},\\\\nonumber\\\\\\\\\\n  \\\\Jarl/\\\\Jarl^{\\\\rm target}&\\\\simeq0.999973,\\n  \\\\label{eq:attractor-fit-reproduced}\\n\\\\end{align}\\nunder the moment-map observable.  We then tested whether it is selected by direct attractor closures.\\n\\n\\\\subsection{Closure tests}\\n\\nThe residual for a closure condition is defined as the normalized squared distance of $T(\\\\Psi)$ from the proposed target span.  Four closures were tested.\\n\\n\\\\paragraph{Self-attractor closure.}\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  T(\\\\Psi_u)\\\\in\\\\Span\\\\{\\\\Psi_u\\\\},\\n  \\\\qquad\\n  T(\\\\Psi_d)\\\\in\\\\Span\\\\{\\\\Psi_d\\\\}.\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nAt the CKM point,\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  R_{\\\\rm self}\\\\simeq2.0018259094.\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nOptimizing the residual selected\\n\\\\begin{align}\\n  r&\\\\simeq0.9669745469+0.0531135081i,\\\\nonumber\\\\\\\\\\n  s&\\\\simeq0.3274287194-0.3362472833i,\\n\\\\end{align}\\nwith CKM error $\\\\simeq0.1391$ and $\\\\Jarl/\\\\Jarl^{\\\\rm target}\\\\simeq0.0634$.\\n\\n\\\\paragraph{Coupled-plane attractor closure.}\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  T(\\\\Psi_u),T(\\\\Psi_d)\\\\in\\\\Span\\\\{\\\\Psi_u,\\\\Psi_d\\\\}.\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nAt the CKM point,\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  R_{\\\\rm plane}\\\\simeq6.9566846713.\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nThe best search collapsed near identity mixing, with CKM error $\\\\simeq0.3250$ and essentially zero CP.\\n\\n\\\\paragraph{Primitive fixed-charge closure.}\\nLet\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\Gamma_u=(1,1,J_u,\\\\bar J_u),\\n  \\\\qquad\\n  \\\\Gamma_d=(1,1,J_d,\\\\bar J_d).\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nThe closure condition is\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  T(\\\\Psi_u),T(\\\\Psi_d)\\\\in\\\\Span\\\\{\\\\Gamma_u,\\\\Gamma_d\\\\}.\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nAt the CKM point,\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  R_{\\\\rm prim}\\\\simeq2.6022987358.\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nThe best search was almost real/no-CP, with CKM error $\\\\simeq0.2191$.\\n\\n\\\\paragraph{Primitive scalar-matched charge closure.}\\nHere the primitive charges share the scalar slots:\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\Gamma_u(a_u)=(a_u,\\\\bar a_u,J_u,\\bar J_u),\\n  \\\\qquad\\n  \\\\Gamma_d(a_d)=(a_d,\\bar a_d,J_d,\\bar J_d).\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nAt the CKM point the residual is again\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  R\\\\simeq2.6022987358.\\n\\\\end{equation}\\nThe best search reduced the CKM magnitude error to $\\\\simeq0.0817$ but over-produced CP:\\n\\\\begin{equation}\\n  \\\\Jarl/\\\\Jarl^{\\\\rm target}\\\\simeq8.82.\\n\\\\end{equation}\\n\\n\\\\subsection{Attractor verdict}\\n\\nThe full direct attractor gate is negative:\\n\\\\begin{center}\\n\\\\fbox{\\\\parbox{0.88\\\\linewidth}{\\nThe generic Freudenthal attractor closure, even with complex scalar slots and primitive charge spans, does not select the CKM-fitting $r,s$.  A genuine derivation would require an additional physically justified boundary charge or potential.\\n}}\\n\\\\end{center}\\n\\n\\\\section{Interpretation}\\n\\\\label{sec:interpretation}\\n\\nThe tested structure separates cleanly into three layers.\\n\\n\\\\begin{enumerate}[label=(\\\\arabic*)]\\n  \\\\item \\\\textbf{Orbit geometry.}  The $E_7/F_4$ orbit supplies kinematics and admissible state geometry.  It is too large by itself to select $r,s$: $\\\\dim(E_7)-\\\\dim(F_4)=133-52=81$.\\n  \\\\item \\\\textbf{Two-Higgs/GUT boundary data.}  The fitted coefficients behave as a two-sector Higgs-basis matrix $C$ with nontrivial rephasing-invariant phase and singular-value ratio.  This is where the CKM phase is localized.\\n  \\\\item \\\\textbf{Attractor dynamics.}  The direct Freudenthal attractor map is the natural dynamical selector, but the closures tested here do not choose the fitted matrix $C$.\\n\\\\end{enumerate}\\n\\nIn physical terms, the result resembles the following situation.  The exceptional moment-map observable identifies the correct kind of complex ``instrument tuning'': the up-type and down-type Jordan/Yukawa structures must be mixed inside the same FTS Jordan slots.  However, the instrument is not yet tuned by the generic attractor equations.  A further boundary principle, possibly from a larger GUT/Higgs potential or a constrained charge orbit, would be needed.\\n\\n\\\\section{Conclusion}\\n\\\\label{sec:conclusion}\\n\\nWe have tested a concrete exceptional-algebraic path toward CKM mixing.  The compact Freudenthal moment map over $J_3(\\\\OO)$ is a viable observable map, and complex tau-real Jordan-slot mixing reproduces CKM to numerical precision.
